Study withdrawal = 3 pt. Conclusions: This 90-day preliminary report suggests the safety of the steroid-free IS used (TAC, MMF, 3-dose) in the trial. The very low ACR rate is of significance, since most acute rejection occurs early after transplantation. The low HCVR is also encouraging, and may be related to the low incidence of acute rejection and steroid free therapy, but much longer followup is needed. A first interim analysis of the treatment groups will be available at the presentation. Background: Living donor liver transplantation has played important role for patients with end stage viral hepatitis because of cadaveric organ shortage. However preliminary results indicate that live liver donation might be disadvantageous for hepatitis C virus (HCV)-positive patients. Material and Methods: Twenty patients who underwent living donor liver transplantation for HCV cirrhosis was the subject of the study. All the patients preemptively received antiviral therapy consisting of interferon -alpha2b and ribavirin, which started around one month after the operation. When HCV-RNA turned negative after the therapy, the therapy was continued for another 12 months. Thereafter the patient was observed without the therapy for 6 months. The patients dropped from the protocol when they could not continue the therapy for 12 months for adverse effects Results: Five patients stopped the therapy, nine responded the therapy and the other 6 did not respond and sustained viral response ratio was 45% (9/20). There was a significant difference between responders and nonresponders in histological activity score after the therapy. The cumulated 3-year survival of the HCV positive patients was 85%, which was comparable with that of hepatitis C virus negative patients (n=93, 90%). Conclusions: Preemptive antiviral therapy after transplantation is safe and might be useful for satisfactory results after living donor liver transplantation for HCV positive patients. Ashok Jain 1 , Raman Venkataramanan 3 , Bijan Eghtesad 2 , Randeep Kashyap 1 , Barbara Yelochan 2 , Amadeo Marcos 2 , John Fung. 1 Surgery, University of Rochester, Rochester, NY, USA; 2 Surgery, T.E.Starzl Transplantation Institute, Pittsburgh, PA, USA; 3 Pharmaceutical Sciences, University of Pittsburgh, Pittsburgh, PA, USA Introduction: Hepatitis C viral infection (HCV) is the commonest indication for liver transplantation (LTx). Recurrence of HCV is uniform after transplantation. Combination of pegylated interferon (peg-INF) with Ribavirin, which is not without the side effects, has been used as anti HCV treatment. It has been recommended that patients with renal dysfunction should receive lower doses of Ribavirin in order to reduce the incidence of hemolysis. Aim of the present study is to examine the role of measurement of plasma and whole blood concentration of Ribavirin to determine this relationship to hemolysis, renal dysfunction, and treatment response. Material: The left over 34-blood sample drawn for tacrolimus level from 23 post LTx patients (who were on Ribavirin) were used to estimate Ribavirin concentration in plasma (all samples) and blood (17 samples) by HPLC. Patients clinical history and concurrent medications were evaluated. Results: There was a wide variation in the Ribavirin concentration ranging from 1.8 /l to 122.1 /l with mean plasma concentration of 48.4± 10.2 /l. There was a close correlation between the plasma and whole blood Ribavirin level (mean plasma level 42.7± 21.8 /l; mean blood level 37.5 ± 17.3 /l.) No correlation was found in the response rate (biochemical, histogical or HCV viral load), hemolysis, renal function or length of Ribavirin treatment on subsequent estimations. However the concentrations were higher when subjects were on antiretroviral agents (5 samples mean 87.3± 39.4 /l) and lower when patients were on proton pump inhibitors (11 samples mean 29.8±20.3 /l). Conclusion: Despite of the fact that Ribavirin is highly bound to red blood cells, the concentration in whole blood and plasma were similar. Higher concentrations were observed with concurrent use of anti retroviral agents and lower with proton pump inhibiter. The toxicity to the concentration could not be established in this pilot study. It appears that Ribavirin, as a parent compound may not be responsible for therapeutic effect or hemolysis. It is possible that its phosphorelated metabolite of Ribavirin may be determining factor to response rate and toxicity. Further more studies are needed to elucidate the role Ribavirin with peg-INF in recurrent HCV post liver transplantation. Kunitada Shimotohno 1 , Koichi Watashi 1 , Makoto Hijikata 1 . 1 Viral Oncology, Institute for Virus Research, Kyoto University, Kyoto, Kyoto, Japan Recurrence of chronic hepatitis C is apparent in approximately 50% of HCV-infected recipients in the first postoperative year. To reduce the rate of the recurrence, patients may receive anti-HCV therapy before or after transplantation. Currently available drugs such as interferon and ribavirin is unable to eliminate HCV in the liver transplant setting, suggesting that indefinite treatment to suppress the effects of virus may be necessary. We have screened candidates for anti-HCV function and found that cyclosporin A (CsA) showed strong suppressive activity to HCV proliferation. Because CsA has been using as an immuno-supressant that targets calcineurin in patients who underwent liver transplantation, we analyzed the molecular mechanism of the anti-HCV function of CsA. Treatment the HCV genome self-replicating cells with CsA for 7 days decreased the amount of HCV RNA to undetectable levels. However, reduction of HCV RNA was not observed after treatment with FK506. The inhibitory effect of CsA on HCV genome replication was also observed in cells infected with HCV. These results suggested that CsA but not FK506 inhibited the replication of HCV genome. To clarify how CsA exerts anti-HCV activity in cultured hepatocytes, we used a reporter assay to examine the transcriptional activity of NF-AT in HCV gennomu replicating cells. Although CsA treatment suppressed NF-AT activity in T lymphocytes as reported previously, it had no effect on NF-AT activity in hepatocyte-derived cells. This suggested that calcineurin-inducible signaling pathways, including the NF-AT pathway, were not related to the anti-HCV activity of CsA in hepatocytes. This conclusion was further supported by an analysis of HCV replication using the CsA derivatives NIM811which does not inhibit calcineurin but has retains the ability to interact with cyclophilins. These data, together with the previous data obtained in hepatocytes indicated that the inhibitory function of CsA was mediated by a mechanism independent of its immunosuppressive function, suggesting that cyclophilin(s) plays important role in regulation of HCV genomu replication. Thus, identification of a cyclophilin that is essential for replication of the HCV genome sheds further light on the mechanism of HCV replication. Furthermore, our data showing an inhibitory effect of CsA on HCV genome replication highlight the importance of selecting an appropriate immunosuppressive agent in liver transplant recipients at increased risk of recurrent HCV infection. Introduction: Patients with chronic Hepatitis C (HCV) that receive liver transplantation uniformly become reinfected. The effect that inflammatory and regenerative cytokines has on HCV association with the liver has not been studied. We hypothesize that infectious HCV will associate with HepG2 cells cultured as spheroids, and this will be potentiated by the addition of interleukin-6 and tumor necrosis factor-alpha. Methods: HepG2 human hepatoma cells were obtained from the American Type Culture Collection (ATCC) and cultured at 3.0x10 5 cells/ml in ATCC recommended medium. For spheroid formation, the cells were cultured on an orbital shaker at 55 RPM. Infectious HCV serum was added to the culture conditions for 8 hours and then washed. IL-6 (1 and 5 ng/ml) and/or TNF-alpha (1 ng/ml) were added for the 8 hour inoculation period. The cells were harvested at 3 and 5 days after inoculation. RNA was extracted. The 5' UTR of the virus was amplified by PCR and resolved by gel electrophoresis. Results: HepG2 cells assumed spheroid formation after 3 days in rotational culture. HepG2 spheroids supported viral association and persisted for 3 and 5 days after inoculation, but there was no detectable virus in the supernatant/culture medium. However, cells inoculated with virus and IL-6 at 1 ng/ml demonstrated viral association and persistence of the virus in the supernatant. IL-6 at 5 ng/ml abrogated viral association or persistence at both harvest dates. Cells inoculated with TNF-alpha permitted viral association at 3 days in culture, but there was no detectable virus at 5 days in culture. This effect of attenuating viral persistence was also seen when the cells were treated with both IL-6 (1ng/ml) and TNF-alpha (1ng/ml). Discussion: HepG2 cells modified by medium additives have been shown to bind HCV, and the induction of spheroid formation alone appears to confer a phenotype that permits viral association and persistence in our study. Viral particles persisted in the supernatant of the samples treated with low dose IL-6, suggesting either that the infected cells were releasing viral progeny or that the cytokine stabilized the virus in the medium. However, at higher doses or with the addition of TNF-alpha viral association and persistence were attenuated. These findings suggest that the regenerative cytokines can alter the association of HCV with the host in a dose dependent manner and requires further study. Background: Adult to adult living donor liver transplantation (ALDLT) is an accepted treatment for patients with end-stage liver disease. However, recipient's post-operative course is not always satisfactory because of detrimental factors, such as small for size graft. Meanwhile, it is conceivable that recipient's pre-operative condition as well as graft volume affects post-operative clinical course. We report the impact of pre-operative recipient's condition and graft size upon post-operative clinical course. Patients and Method: Between September 1997 and December 2003, 103 patients underwent ALDLT in Hokkaido University Hospital. Of the total number of liver transplant patients, twenty six pediatric patients and sixteen patients whose primary disease was fluminant hepatic failure were excluded from this study. Data from the remnant 61 transplants were retrospectively analyzed. Graft size was standardized by the ratio of graft volume to standard liver volume (GV/SV ratio). Model of End Stage Liver Disease score (MELD score) was used as index of pre-operative recipient's condition. Peak level of total bilirubin after the operation (peak T-bil) was used as index of graft function. Results: MELD score divided by GV/SV ratio was significantly higher in mortality group than in survival group. Conclusion: Not only graft size but pre-operative recipients' condition influenced postoperative recipient's condition in ALDLT. The recipient whose pre-operative condition is poor requires larger graft for uneventful course after transplantation. MELD score divided by GV/SV ratio correctly reflects the post-operative recipient's recovery in ALDLT. Background: MELD scores have been used as indicator for cadaveric liver allocation in the United States. Recently, the applicability of MELD score as predictor of the outcomes after liver transplantation was reported. It is, however, controversial whether MELD score can predict the outcomes after adult-to-adult living donor liver transplantation (LDLT). In this study, we tested whether MELD score and other preoperative variables can predict short term mortality after right-lobe LDLT for adult recipients. Methods: Between 1994 and 2003, 249 patients underwent right-lobe LDLT at our institute. A total of 204 recipients were enrolled, after excluding 45 transplantations for fulminant hepatic failure and re-transplantation. We defined a subject who died within 90 days after LDLT. All recipients were categorized into two groups according to MELD score, Group A (n=140): MELD score <25; and Group B (n=64): 25≤ MELD. MELD groups, as well as 21 preoperative variables, such as etiology, blood mismatch, and laboratory data, were analyzed by Cox proportional hazard regression method. Results: A total of 37 patients (20 in Group A, 17 in Group B) died within 90 days after right-lobe LDLT. Cox proportional hazard regression demonstrated that MELD group was a significant determinant for 90-day mortality (p=0.045, Fig.1 ). Among preoperative variables, past history of upper abdominal operation (p=0.009) was significantly associated with 90-day mortality in Group A, and treatment with continuous hemodiafiltration (p=0.017) was significantly associated in Group B. The present study demonstrated that MELD score is a good predictor for 90-day mortality in our right-lobe LDLT series. However, additional risk factors also affect the 90-day survivals of the recipients in each MELD group. This suggests that other parameters in addition to MELD score may be required to predict the outcomes after LDLT more accurately. To present an experience with the indication of right lobe graft with middle hepatic vein in adult living donor liver transplantation (LDLT). Summary background data: There remains a major controversy that the venous drainage from the anterior segment substantially depends on tributaries of the middle hepatic vein (MHV), and deprivation of such tributaries into the MHV may critically influence the postoperative graft function. Right lobe with MHV could be a resolution for the potential problem of congestion in the anterior segment. Methods: From December 2000 to October 2003, we performed 171 right lobe LDLTs for adult patients. Of these, 28 patients received a right lobe with MHV graft (16.4%). Over the period reported, technical modification in donor operation with a computer-assisted volumetric analysis according to the hepatic venous anatomy (preserving the proximal side of the MHV and the drainage vein of segment 4b to the MHV). Results: The overall cumulative 1-year graft survival rate of right lobe with MHV (n=28) and right lobe without MHV (n=143) were 82.2% and 76.8% (p=NS). The proximal side of the MHV and the drainage vein of segment 4b to the MHV was preserved in 16 patients according to the regional volume of V4b in the remnant donor liver. All of them need venous interposition graft for MHV anastomosis. Three donors experienced complications that required treatment, including 2 cases of biliary leakage and one of liver failure due to non-alcholic steatohepatitis. All patients had a patent right hepatic vein and MHV anastomosis during the follow-up period. There were no complications related to the hepatic vein anastomosis. The optimization of venous drainage in a right liver graft through the middle hepatic vein (MHV) can induce segment IV congestion in the donor. The aim of this study was to evaluate the prevalence of early segment IV congestion following MHV deprivation according to the related venous anatomy, with its consequences on biological, clinical and volumetric outcome in donors. Between 1998 and 2003, 47 living-donor liver transplantations were performed using a right graft and 11 donors without MHV harvesting (MHV-) were compared to 17 donors with MHV harvesting (MHV+). According to the left liver venous drainage, segment IV was entirely drained through the MHV in 8 (29%) patients and only partially in other cases. Biological, clinical outcome and volumetric measurement were compared according to the degree of venous congestion, defined as global (GC), partial (PC) or no congestion (NC). The remnant liver-to-body weight ratio (DRV) was calculated one week postoperatively using CT volumetric assessment divided by donor's body weight. Venous congestion never occurred in MHV-group. In the MHV+ group, 14 (82%) of patients experienced congestion which was global in 7 (50%) patients. Segment IV was entirely or mostly drained in MHV in all of them. The remaining 7 (50%) patients had only partial congestion. Among them, segment IV was equally drained through left and MHV in 4 (57%). Overall, a preserved scissural vein was often seen in patients who had partial or no congestion. Prothrombin rate was significantly lower in GC group as compared to NC group on postoperative day 1 and 5 (50 vs. 62% and 76 vs. 86%, respectively). Overall morbidity was similar in the MHV-group as compared to the MHV+ group (82% vs 53%, respectively, p=ns) and between GC, PC and NC groups (57% vs 57%vs 71% respectively,p=ns). The DRV was similar at one week in GC, PC and NC groups (1.40+/ -0.10 vs 1.41+/-0.29 vs 1.25+/-0.32 respectively, p=ns for all). CONCLUSION This study shows that early segment IV congestion in donor is common after MHV harvesting and that its magnitude and location can be predicted by the venous anatomy. Entire segment IV venous drainage through MHV is predictive of global congestion, which is associated with a decrease in early postoperative prothrombin rate. Thus, we suggest avoidance of MHV harvesting in donors with critical remnant liver volume and segment IV entirely drained through the MHV. Background. Although several reports claim that portal hypertension after liver transplantation (LT) adversely affects graft function, few reports have assessed the impact of portal venous pressure (PVP) on graft regeneration. We therefore analyzed the impact of PVP after living-donor liver transplantation (LDLT) to adult recipients on regeneration and the graft damage. Methods. Between March 2002 and December 2003, 30 adult recipients underwent LDLT in our institution. We divided them into 2 groups based on mean PVP monitored through a catheter inserted via the inferior mesenteric vein during 3 days after LT: higher portal pressure group with a PVP≥20 mmHg (Group H; n=16), and a lower portal pressure group with a PVP<20 mmHg (Group L; n=14). Adult to adult living donor liver transplantation (AALDTx) remains controversial and recent reports are contradictory regarding the cost of this procedure. We compared all hospital direct costs for recipients from one month prior to transplant to one year after transplant for 75 deceased donor transplants (DDLTx) and compared these with 26 AALDTx performed over the same time period. Activated protein C (APC) has shown anticoagulant and anti-inflammatory effects during reperfusion in animals models. Carranza 2 , Chanjong Chung 3 . 1 Anesthesiology, Thomas Jefferson University, Philadelphia, PA, USA; 2 Anesthesiology, Hospital Central Militar, Mexico City, Mexico; 3 Anesthesiology, Donga University, Pusan, Korea Purpose: The purpose of this retrospective study was to investigate whether the presence of fibrinolysis can be diagnosed in its early stage by comparing the thromboelastographic (TEG) progression of untreated blood and blood-treated with e-aminocaproic acid (EACA). Methods: Intraoperative coagulation profiles and TEG of 925 patients undergoing liver transplantation were reviewed after the approval of the IRRB. Patients (n=113) without clot formation on TEG were excluded because of potential combined effects of fibrinolysis and heparin. Results: All TEG variables improved in most patients of both groups of patients. The area under the curve (AUC) of TEG of EACA-treated blood was greater than untreated blood in both groups of patients, but its increase was more pronounced in the Lysis group patients. In conclusion, the presence of fibrinolysis can be detected within 30 min by the rapid improvement in EACA-treated blood. Introduction: This randomized prospective double-blind study was designed to test the hypothesis that the perioperative infusion of fenoldopam provides renal protection during liver transplantation. Methods: The study protocol was approved by the IRB and informed consent was obtained from all patients. Patients with initial serum creatinine levels of > 2.0 mg/dl were excluded. The study drug infusion was initiated to provide a dose of fenoldopam of 0.03 mcg/kg/min in the study group. This was titrated up to a maximum dose of 0.15 mcg/ kg/min as hemodynamics permitted. Renal function was assessed by determining the patient's serum creatinine immediately preoperatively and comparing these results with a repeated analysis 24 hours postoperatively. Orthotopic liver transplantation was performed in a standard fashion with venovenous bypass. Statistical analysis included repeated measures analysis of variance followed up with 2 sample and paired t-tests. (P-value < 0.05 significant) Results: A total of 38 patients were enrolled into the study: 21 patients into the fenoldopam group and 17 patients into the placebo group. (Introduction) Biliary complications including anastomotic leakage and stricture were considered as troublesome problems in duct-to-duct anastomosis of adult living donor liver transplantation. So, various technical modifications were attempted to reduce biliary complications and to perform easy and comfortable biliary recontruction in two or more ducts in graft.(Purpose) We introduced a new high hilar Glissonian dissection technique in recipient hepatectomy for reducing biliary complications in adult living donor liver transplnation and compared biliary complications between a conventional method and a new method using high hilar Glissonian dissection in biliary reconstruction. (Methods) From August 2000 to June 2003, 98 patients received adult LDLT using duct-to-duct anastomosis of biliary reconstruction in our center. They were divided into group 1 (n=70) using conventional method for biliary reconstruction of duct-to-duct anastomosis and group 2 (n= 28) using a new high hilar Glissonian dissection technique. After Pringles' maneuver, Glissonian pedicles were cut at the high hilar(intrahepatic) level. After that, the portal vein was separated from the Glissonian pedicles. Using this new technique, we could get longer portal vein, hepatic artery, and bile duct, and save the blood supply to the end of bile duct. The duct-to-duct anastomosis could be performed without tension and ischemia. (Results) There were 77 males (78.6%)and 21 females(21.4%), and their mean age was 46.4 years. Mean follow-up duration was 17.8 months. The overall biliary complication rate was 21.4 % in group 1 and 14.3% in group 2 (p>0.05). Bile leakage from anastomosis in group 1 was 4.3% , but, there was no leakge in group group 2(p>0.05). Also, stricture of anastomotic site were occurred 17.1% in group 1 and 7.1% in group 2, respectively(p>0.05). (Conclusions) Although the incidence of biliary complications was not significantly decreased statistically after introduction of a high hilar dissection technique, we consider this method as a very feasible technique for biliary reconstruction in duct-toduct anastomosis. Anatomy of the bile duct in the donor was evaluated by pre-operative CT or MR cholangiography and intraoperative cholangiography. The graft had a single orifice in 7 cases, two orifices that could be made to one with back table plasty in 8 cases. The other six cases needed two separate anastomoses. In the 4 of 6 cases, two orifices of the graft bile duct were too much separated (more than 1 cm) to be reconstructed by the stump of the hepatic ducts. For one of two orifices, stump of the recipient' cystic duct was used. All the 4 recipients were male with a mean age of 41.5 years (range 16-58). Average follow period was nine months (range 3-16). The indicated diseases were hepatitis C cirrhosis in 2, hepatitis B cirrhosis in 1 and Caloli disease in 1. All recipients were ABO-identical with donors. The anastomosis was performed by interrupted suture using 6/0 PDS with an external stent tube. Remnant of the recipients' cystic duct was left longer, and plastied to a roll for the reconstruction. The stent tube was kept unremoved at least three months after transplantation. (Results) Post-transplant cholangiography performed one month after transplantation showed a good passage in all cases without any anastomotic stenosis or bile leakage. One recipient died of chronic rejection, but the other three have been doing well without graft dysfunction. (Conclusion) Cystic duct is useful in the reconstruction of multiple bile ducts in right lobe living donor liver transplantation.
